2026-03-16T01:02:39.2281510Z copilot: Now I know the waypoint structure:
2026-03-16T01:02:39.2282739Z 1. The player sets a waypoint on the map → `CRadar::SetCoordBlip(BLIP_COORD, pos, ..., "CODEWAY")` is called
2026-03-16T01:02:39.2283440Z 2. Then `CRadar::SetBlipSprite(handle, RADAR_SPRITE_WAYPOINT)` is called (sprite 41)
2026-03-16T01:02:39.2283933Z 3. The blip handle is stored in `m_nTargetBlipIndex`
2026-03-16T01:02:39.2284162Z 
2026-03-16T01:02:39.2284260Z So the waypoint blip has:
2026-03-16T01:02:39.2284544Z - `m_nRadarSprite == RADAR_SPRITE_WAYPOINT` (41)
2026-03-16T01:02:39.2284773Z 
2026-03-16T01:02:39.2284777Z 
2026-03-16T01:02:39.2284867Z - `m_nBlipType == BLIP_COORD` (4)
2026-03-16T01:02:39.2285112Z - `m_bInUse == 1`
2026-03-16T01:02:39.2285238Z 
2026-03-16T01:02:39.2286151Z To find the waypoint position, I need to search through the radar trace array for an entry that's in use and has either the waypoint sprite or the map marker sprite, with the coordinate blip type. Alternatively, I could check the target blip index directly.
2026-03-16T01:02:39.2287550Z 
2026-03-16T01:02:39.2288878Z Looking at the code flow more carefully, when a waypoint is set, it first clears any existing target blip, then creates a new coordinate blip and sets its sprite to the waypoint sprite. So I should be looking for a blip with sprite type 41 and the coordinate blip type. Let me trace through the blip handle format to understand how the indices work.
